<p><b>Asturias</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/æ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">æ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span><span title="/ʊər/: &#39;our&#39; in &#39;tour&#39;">ʊər</span><span title="/i/: &#39;y&#39; in &#39;happy&#39;">i</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span></span>,<span class="wrap"> </span><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span></span>-/</a></span></span>,<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> <small>Spanish:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[asˈtuɾjas]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Asturian_language" title="Asturian language">Asturian</a>: <i lang="ast">Asturies</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Astur-Leonese" title="Help:IPA/Astur-Leonese">[asˈtuɾjes; -ɾjɪs]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Galician-Asturian" title="Galician-Asturian">Eonaviego</a>: Asturias), officially the <b>Principality of Asturias</b> (<a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <i lang="es">Principado de Asturias</i>; <a href="/wiki/Asturian_language" title="Asturian language">Asturian</a>: <i lang="ast">Principáu d'Asturies</i>), is an <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_communities_of_Spain" title="Autonomous communities of Spain">autonomous community</a> in north-west <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>. It is coextensive with the <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Spain" title="Provinces of Spain">province</a> of Asturias, and contains some of the territory that was part of the larger <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Asturias" title="Kingdom of Asturias">Kingdom of Asturias</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>. Divided into eight <a href="/wiki/Comarcas_of_Asturias" title="Comarcas of Asturias"><i>comarcas</i></a> (counties), the autonomous community of Asturias is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Cantabria" title="Cantabria">Cantabria</a> to the east, by <a href="/wiki/Le%C3%B3n,_Spain" title="León, Spain">León</a> (<a href="/wiki/Castile_and_Le%C3%B3n" title="Castile and León">Castile and León</a>) to the south, by <a href="/wiki/Lugo" title="Lugo">Lugo</a> (<a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">Galicia</a>) to the west, and by the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Biscay" title="Bay of Biscay">Bay of Biscay</a> (<a href="/wiki/Cantabrian_Sea" title="Cantabrian Sea">Cantanbric sea</a>) to the north.
</p><p>The most important cities are the communal capital, <a href="/wiki/Oviedo" title="Oviedo">Oviedo</a> (<i>Uviéu</i>), the seaport and largest city <a href="/wiki/Gij%C3%B3n" title="Gijón">Gijón</a> (<i>Xixón</i>), and the industrial town of <a href="/wiki/Avil%C3%A9s" title="Avilés">Avilés</a>. Other <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_in_Asturias" title="List of municipalities in Asturias">municipalities in Asturias</a> include <a href="/wiki/Cangas_de_On%C3%ADs" title="Cangas de Onís">Cangas de Onís</a> (<i>Cangues d'Onís</i>), <a href="/wiki/Cangas_del_Narcea" title="Cangas del Narcea">Cangas del Narcea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goz%C3%B3n" title="Gozón">Gozón</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grado,_Asturias" title="Grado, Asturias">Grado</a> (<i>Grau</i> or <i>Grao</i>), <a href="/wiki/Langreo" title="Langreo">Langreo</a> (<i>Llangréu</i>), <a href="/wiki/Llanera,_Asturias" title="Llanera, Asturias">Llanera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Laviana" title="Laviana">Laviana</a> (<i>Llaviana</i>), <a href="/wiki/Lena,_Asturias" title="Lena, Asturias">Lena</a> (<i>Ḷḷena</i>), <a href="/wiki/Llanes" title="Llanes">Llanes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mieres,_Asturias" class="mw-redirect" title="Mieres, Asturias">Mieres</a>, <a href="/wiki/Siero" title="Siero">Siero</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vald%C3%A9s,_Asturias" title="Valdés, Asturias">Valdés</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vegadeo" title="Vegadeo">Vegadeo</a> (<i>A Veiga</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Villaviciosa,_Asturias" title="Villaviciosa, Asturias">Villaviciosa</a> (<i>see also <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_in_Asturias" title="List of municipalities in Asturias">List of municipalities</a> and <a href="/wiki/Comarcas_of_Asturias" title="Comarcas of Asturias">comarcas in Asturias</a></i>).
</p><p>Asturias is also home of the <a href="/wiki/Princess_of_Asturias_Awards" title="Princess of Asturias Awards">Princess of Asturias Awards</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturias&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Termes_romanes_de_Gij%C3%B3n_03.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Termes_romanes_de_Gij%C3%B3n_03.JPG/170px-Termes_romanes_de_Gij%C3%B3n_03.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Termes_romanes_de_Gij%C3%B3n_03.JPG/255px-Termes_romanes_de_Gij%C3%B3n_03.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Termes_romanes_de_Gij%C3%B3n_03.JPG/340px-Termes_romanes_de_Gij%C3%B3n_03.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Termes_romanes_de_Gij%C3%B3n_03.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Roman thermae in Gijón</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Asturian_architecture" title="Asturian architecture">Asturian architecture</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_castros_in_Asturias&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="List of castros in Asturias (page does not exist)">List of castros in Asturias</a></div>
<p>Asturias was inhabited, first by <i><a href="/wiki/Homo_erectus" title="Homo erectus">Homo erectus</a></i>, then by <a href="/wiki/Neanderthals" class="mw-redirect" title="Neanderthals">Neanderthals</a>. Since the <a href="/wiki/Lower_Paleolithic" title="Lower Paleolithic">Lower Paleolithic</a> era, and during the <a href="/wiki/Upper_Paleolithic" title="Upper Paleolithic">Upper Paleolithic</a>, Asturias was characterized by cave paintings in the eastern part of the area. In the <a href="/wiki/Mesolithic" title="Mesolithic">Mesolithic</a> period, a native culture developed, that of the <i>Asturiense</i>, and later, with the introduction of the <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a>, <a href="/wiki/Megalith" title="Megalith">megaliths</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tumulus" title="Tumulus">tumuli</a> were constructed. In the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a>, the territory came under the cultural influence of the <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celts</a>; the local Celtic peoples, known as the <a href="/wiki/Astur" class="mw-redirect" title="Astur">Astures</a>, were composed of tribes such as the <i>Luggones</i>, the <i>Pesicos</i>, and others, who populated the entire area with <i><a href="/wiki/Castro_(village)" class="mw-redirect" title="Castro (village)">castros</a></i> (fortified hill-towns). Today the <a href="/wiki/Astur" class="mw-redirect" title="Astur">Astur</a> Celtic influence persists in <a href="/wiki/Toponym" class="mw-redirect" title="Toponym">place names</a>, such as those of rivers and mountains.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Iglesia_de_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_del_Naranco.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Iglesia_de_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_del_Naranco.jpg/220px-Iglesia_de_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_del_Naranco.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Iglesia_de_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_del_Naranco.jpg/330px-Iglesia_de_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_del_Naranco.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Iglesia_de_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_del_Naranco.jpg/440px-Iglesia_de_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_del_Naranco.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Iglesia_de_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_del_Naranco.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Santa María del Naranco, ancient palace of Asturian Kings, 842 AD. Many churches of Asturias are among the <a href="/wiki/List_of_oldest_church_buildings#Late_Antiquity_and_Early_Middle_Ages" title="List of oldest church buildings">oldest churches of Europe since Early Middle Ages</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>With the conquest of Asturias by the <a href="/wiki/Roman_empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman empire">Romans</a> under <a href="/wiki/Caesar_Augustus" class="mw-redirect" title="Caesar Augustus">Augustus</a> (29–19 BC), the region entered into recorded history. The Astures were subdued by the Romans but were never fully conquered. After several centuries without foreign presence, they enjoyed a brief revival during the Germanic invasions of the late 4th century AD, resisting <a href="/wiki/Suebi" title="Suebi">Suevi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Visigoths" title="Visigoths">Visigoth</a> raids throughout the 5th Century AD, ending with the <a href="/wiki/Moorish_invasion_of_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Moorish invasion of Spain">Moorish invasion of Spain</a>. However, as it had been for the Romans and Visigoths, the Moors did not find mountainous territory easy to conquer, and the lands along Spain's northern coast never fully became part of <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">Islamic Spain</a>. Rather, with the beginning of the Moorish conquest in the 8th century, this region became a refuge for Christian nobles, and in 722, a <i>de facto</i> independent kingdom was established, the <i><a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Asturias" title="Kingdom of Asturias">Regnum Asturorum</a></i>, which was to become the cradle of the incipient <i><a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">Reconquista</a></i> (Reconquest).
</p><p>In the 10th century, the Kingdom of Asturias gave way to the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Le%C3%B3n" title="Kingdom of León">Kingdom of León</a>, and during the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> the geographic isolation of the territory made historical references scarce. Through the rebellion of <a href="/wiki/Henry_II_of_Castile" title="Henry II of Castile">Henry II of Castile</a> in the 14th century, the Principality of Asturias was established. The most famous proponents of independence were Gonzalo Peláez and <a href="/wiki/Queen_Urraca" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen Urraca">Queen Urraca</a>, who, while achieving significant victories, were ultimately defeated by <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">Castilian</a> troops. After its integration into the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Spain">Kingdom of Spain</a>, Asturias provided the Spanish court with high-ranking aristocrats and played an important role in the colonisation of America. Since 1388, the heir to the Castilian (later Spanish) throne has been styled <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Asturias" title="Prince of Asturias">Prince of Asturias</a>. In the 16th century, the population reached 100,000 for the first time, and within another century that number would double due to the arrival of American <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">corn</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Francisco_de_Goya_y_Lucientes_-_Gaspar_Melchor_de_Jovellanos.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Francisco_de_Goya_y_Lucientes_-_Gaspar_Melchor_de_Jovellanos.jpg/170px-Francisco_de_Goya_y_Lucientes_-_Gaspar_Melchor_de_Jovellanos.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="267" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Francisco_de_Goya_y_Lucientes_-_Gaspar_Melchor_de_Jovellanos.jpg/255px-Francisco_de_Goya_y_Lucientes_-_Gaspar_Melchor_de_Jovellanos.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Francisco_de_Goya_y_Lucientes_-_Gaspar_Melchor_de_Jovellanos.jpg/340px-Francisco_de_Goya_y_Lucientes_-_Gaspar_Melchor_de_Jovellanos.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1939" data-file-height="3051" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Francisco_de_Goya_y_Lucientes_-_Gaspar_Melchor_de_Jovellanos.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Gaspar Melchor de Jovellanos</div></div></div>
<p>In the 18th century, Asturias was one of the centres of the <a href="/wiki/Enlightenment_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Enlightenment Spain">Spanish Enlightenment</a>. The renowned <a href="/wiki/Galician_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Galician people">Galician</a> thinker <a href="/wiki/Benito_Jer%C3%B3nimo_Feij%C3%B3o_y_Montenegro" title="Benito Jerónimo Feijóo y Montenegro">Benito de Feijóo</a> settled in the <a href="/wiki/Benedictine" class="mw-redirect" title="Benedictine">Benedictine</a> <a href="/wiki/Monastery" title="Monastery">Monastery</a> of <a href="/wiki/San_Vicente_de_Oviedo" class="mw-redirect" title="San Vicente de Oviedo">San Vicente de Oviedo</a>. <a href="/wiki/Gaspar_Melchor_de_Jovellanos" title="Gaspar Melchor de Jovellanos">Gaspar Melchor de Jovellanos</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Polymath" title="Polymath">polymath</a> and prominent reformer and politician of the late 18th century, was born in the seaside town of <a href="/wiki/Gij%C3%B3n" title="Gijón">Gijón</a>.
</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>, Asturias was the first Spanish province to rise up against the French following the abdication of King <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_VII_of_Spain" title="Ferdinand VII of Spain">Ferdinand VII</a> on 10 May 1808. Riots began in Oviedo and on 25 May the local government formally declared war on <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a> with 18,000 men called to arms to resist invasion.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a> came to Asturias after 1830 with the discovery and systematic exploitation of coal mines and iron factories at the mining basins of <a href="/wiki/Nal%C3%B3n_(comarca)" title="Nalón (comarca)">Nalón</a> and <a href="/wiki/Caudal_(Asturian_comarca)" class="mw-redirect" title="Caudal (Asturian comarca)">Caudal</a>. At the same time, there was significant migration to <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">the Americas</a> (especially <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">Uruguay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>); those who succeeded overseas often returned to their native land much wealthier. These entrepreneurs were known collectively as 'Indianos', for having visited and made their fortunes in the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a> and beyond. The heritage of these wealthy families can still be seen in Asturias today: many large 'modernista' villas are dotted across the region, as well as cultural institutions such as free schools and public libraries.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NE_800ad.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/NE_800ad.jpg/220px-NE_800ad.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="181" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/NE_800ad.jpg/330px-NE_800ad.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/NE_800ad.jpg/440px-NE_800ad.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1533" data-file-height="1264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NE_800ad.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Location of Asturias and its neighbors in 800 AD</div></div></div>
<p>Asturias played an important part in the events that led up to the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a>. In October 1934 Asturian miners and other workers staged an armed uprising  (see <a href="/wiki/Asturian_miners%27_strike_of_1934" title="Asturian miners&#39; strike of 1934">Revolution of Asturias</a>) to oppose the coming to power of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Confederation_of_the_Autonomous_Right" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish Confederation of the Autonomous Right">right-wing CEDA</a> party, which had obtained three ministerial posts in the centralist government of the <a href="/wiki/Second_Spanish_Republic" title="Second Spanish Republic">Second Spanish Republic</a>. For a month, a Popular Front Committee exercised control in southern Asturias, while local workers committees sprang up elsewhere in the region. A war committee dominated by <a href="/wiki/Anarcho-syndicalist" class="mw-redirect" title="Anarcho-syndicalist">anarcho-syndicalist</a> supporters took power in Oviedo . Troops under the command of a then unknown general named <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">Francisco Franco Bahamonde</a> were brought from <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Morocco" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish Morocco">Spanish Morocco</a> to suppress the revolt. Franco applied tactics normally reserved for overseas colonies, using troops of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Legion" title="Spanish Legion">Spanish Legion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Regulares" title="Regulares">Moroccan troops</a>: ferocious oppression followed.
</p><p>As a result, Asturias remained loyal to the republican government during the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a>, and was the scene of an extraordinary defence in extreme terrain, the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_El_Mazuco" title="Battle of El Mazuco">Battle of El Mazuco</a>. With Franco eventually gaining control of all Spain, Asturias — traditionally linked to the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Crown" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish Crown">Spanish Crown</a> — was known merely as the "Province of Oviedo" from 1939 until Franco's death in 1975. The province's name was restored fully after the return of democracy to Spain, in 1977. In the 50s and 60s the industrial progress of Asturias continued with the constitution of national enterprises like <a href="/wiki/Ensidesa" class="mw-redirect" title="Ensidesa">Ensidesa</a> and Hunosa, but the 80s was the decade of a dramatic <a href="/wiki/Industrial_restructuring" class="mw-redirect" title="Industrial restructuring">industrial restructuring</a>.
</p><p>On 30 December 1981,<sup id="cite_ref-lavozdeasturias_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lavozdeasturias-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Asturias became an autonomous community within the decentralised territorial structure established by the Constitution of 1978. <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Luis_Fern%C3%A1ndez_%C3%81lvarez" class="mw-redirect" title="Rafael Luis Fernández Álvarez">Rafael Luis Fernández Álvarez</a>, who had previously served as the President of the Regional Council since 1978, became the first <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Principality_of_Asturias" title="President of the Principality of Asturias">President of the Principality of Asturias</a>, upon the adoption of autonomy.<sup id="cite_ref-lavozdeasturias_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lavozdeasturias-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_Principality_of_Asturias" class="mw-redirect" title="Government of the Principality of Asturias">Asturian regional government</a> holds comprehensive competencies in important areas such as health, education and protection of the environment. As of May 2011, the President of the Government of Asturias was <a href="/wiki/Francisco_%C3%81lvarez-Cascos" title="Francisco Álvarez-Cascos">Francisco Álvarez-Cascos</a>, of the <a href="/wiki/Foro_Asturias" class="mw-redirect" title="Foro Asturias">Foro Asturias</a> (FAC), followed by <a href="/wiki/Javier_Fern%C3%A1ndez_Fern%C3%A1ndez" class="mw-redirect" title="Javier Fernández Fernández">Javier Fernández</a> (<a href="/wiki/Spanish_Socialist_Workers%27_Party" title="Spanish Socialist Workers&#39; Party">PSOE</a>) in 2012 and the current president is <a href="/wiki/Adri%C3%A1n_Barb%C3%B3n" title="Adrián Barbón">Adrián Barbón</a> (<a href="/wiki/Spanish_Socialist_Workers%27_Party" title="Spanish Socialist Workers&#39; Party">PSOE</a>) elected in 2019.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_and_territorial_division">Administrative and territorial division</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturias&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Administrative and territorial division">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Asturias is organised territorially into 78 <a href="/wiki/Municipality" title="Municipality">municipalities</a>, further subdivided into <a href="/wiki/Parroquia_(Spain)" title="Parroquia (Spain)">parishes</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Municipalities_of_Asturias">Municipalities of Asturias</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturias&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Municipalities of Asturias">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Asturias" class="mw-redirect" title="Municipalities of Asturias">Municipalities of Asturias</a></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parishes">Parishes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturias&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Parishes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Parroquia_(Spain)" title="Parroquia (Spain)">Parroquia (Spain)</a></div>
<p>The parroquia or parish is the subdivision of the Asturian municipalities. Currently, there are 857 parishes integrating the 78 municipalities in the region, and they usually coincide with the ecclesiastic divisions.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_climate">Geography and climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturias&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Geography and climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Picos_Europa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Picos_Europa.jpg/220px-Picos_Europa.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Picos_Europa.jpg/330px-Picos_Europa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Picos_Europa.jpg/440px-Picos_Europa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2595" data-file-height="1732" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Picos_Europa.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Picos de Europa</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cantabrian_Mountains" title="Cantabrian Mountains">Cantabrian Mountains</a> (<i>Cordillera Cantábrica</i>) form Asturias's natural border with the province of <a href="/wiki/Le%C3%B3n_(province)" class="mw-redirect" title="León (province)">León</a> to the south. In the eastern range, the <a href="/wiki/Picos_de_Europa" title="Picos de Europa">Picos de Europa</a> National Park contains the highest and arguably most spectacular mountains, rising to 2,648 metres (8,688&#160;ft) at the Torrecerredo peak. Other notable features of this predominantly limestone range are the <a href="/wiki/Redes_Natural_Park" title="Redes Natural Park">Parque Natural de Redes</a> in the central east, the central Ubiñas south of <a href="/wiki/Oviedo" title="Oviedo">Oviedo</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Somiedo_Natural_Park" title="Somiedo Natural Park">Parque Natural de Somiedo</a> in the west. The Cantabrian mountains offer opportunities for activities such as climbing, walking, skiing and caving, and extend some 200 kilometres (120&#160;mi) in total, as far as <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">Galicia</a> province to the west of Asturias and <a href="/wiki/Cantabria" title="Cantabria">Cantabria</a> province to the east. Similar opportunities are available for the traveler of Asturias interested in <a href="/wiki/Caldoveiro_Peak" title="Caldoveiro Peak">Caldoveiro Peak</a>.
</p><p>The Asturian coastline is extensive, with hundreds of beaches, coves and natural sea caves. Notable examples include the Playa del Silencio (<i>Beach of Silence</i>) near the fishing village of Cudillero (west of <a href="/wiki/Gij%C3%B3n" title="Gijón">Gijón</a>), as well as the many beaches surrounding the summer resort of Llanes, such as the Barro, Ballota and Torimbia (the latter a predominantly <a href="/wiki/Nudist" class="mw-redirect" title="Nudist">nudist</a> beach). Most of Asturias's beaches are sandy, clean, and bordered by steep cliffs, on top of which it is not unusual to see grazing livestock.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Playa_de_Torimbia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Playa_de_Torimbia.jpg/220px-Playa_de_Torimbia.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Playa_de_Torimbia.jpg/330px-Playa_de_Torimbia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Playa_de_Torimbia.jpg/440px-Playa_de_Torimbia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Playa_de_Torimbia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Torimbia beach, <a href="/wiki/Llanes" title="Llanes">Llanes</a></div></div></div>
<p>The key features of Asturian geography are its rugged coastal cliffs and the mountainous interior.
The climate of Asturias is heavily marked by the gulf stream. Falling within the Cantabrian belt known as Green Spain it has high precipitations all year round. Summers are mild and, on the coast, winters also have relatively benign temperatures, rarely including frost. The cold is especially felt in the mountains, where snow is present from October till May. Both rain and snow are regular weather features of Asturian winters. In coastal or near-coastal areas, daytime high temperatures generally average around 12&#160;°C (54&#160;°F) – 13&#160;°C (55&#160;°F) during winter and 22&#160;°C (72&#160;°F) – 23&#160;°C (73&#160;°F) in summer.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table align="center">

<tbody><tr>
<td><div>
<table class="wikitable collapsible collapsed" style="width:100%; text-align:center; line-height: 1.2em; margin:auto;">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Pollution">Pollution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturias&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Pollution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>This part of Spain is one of the most well conserved in the entire country, and full of vegetation and wild spaces. It holds two of the most important natural parks in Spain, and is very renowned for the Picos de Europa and Somiedo areas.
</p><p>The Gijón area was marked and singled out as one of the <a href="/wiki/Pollution" title="Pollution">pollution</a> hotspots in Western Europe in a 2015 report from the International Institute for Applied Science Systems, where predictions for 2030 conditions were made.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Gijón was marked much higher than any other Spanish metro area, in spite of the much larger populations in cities such as <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>. This was attributed to heavy industrial activities. Since outdoor air pollution is a major cause of premature death in Europe,<sup id="cite_ref-Air_-_Environment_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Air_-_Environment-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> the excessive pollution is a major concern for Asturias. The majority of Asturias population live within a 25 kilometres (16&#160;mi) range from the port of Gijón, so pollution would be likely to heavily affect the population.
</p><p>A Spanish government study conducted in 2010 regarding life expectancy in relative communities, Asturias was ranked lowest (tied with <a href="/wiki/Andalucia" class="mw-redirect" title="Andalucia">Andalucia</a>) for male life expectancy with 76.7 years from 2007 readings.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> However, female life expectancy was 84 years and normal among autonomous communities. However, even the male life expectancy is only just below Western European standards, and exaggerated by the high Spanish life expectancy. Considering that many Asturians live in relatively close proximity to Gijón's heavily industrial areas, these figures for especially female relative health still contribute to a position that Gijón is a safe location to live. The numbers for "disability-free" life expectancy has risen significantly both for males and females in the area since 1986, according to the report.<sup id="cite_ref-Air_-_Environment_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Air_-_Environment-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Update: the coal fired electric generating plant, Aboño, completed a Spanish government/EU demand to install equipment to drastically reduce its emissions. Also, the other two major polluters - Arcelor Gijón and Arcelor Avilés - have announced an investment of 100 million euros to do the same. These factories have been a major cause of the area's high airborne pollution.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturias&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<p>In 2017, Asturias had a <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> of 1.03, the lowest in the European Union.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturias&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Asturian_linguistic_areas.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Asturian_linguistic_areas.PNG/220px-Asturian_linguistic_areas.PNG" decoding="async" width="220" height="183" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Asturian_linguistic_areas.PNG/330px-Asturian_linguistic_areas.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Asturian_linguistic_areas.PNG/440px-Asturian_linguistic_areas.PNG 2x" data-file-width="993" data-file-height="824" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Asturian_linguistic_areas.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Language map of Asturias</div></div></div>
<p>The only official language in Asturias is <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Asturian_language" title="Asturian language">Asturian language</a>, also known as Bable, is also spoken, and is protected by law (<i>Ley 1/1998, de 23 de marzo, de uso y promoción del bable/asturiano</i> — "Law 1/1998, of 23 March, of Use and Promotion of Bable/Asturian"). It is sometimes used by the Asturian <a href="/wiki/Civil_service" title="Civil service">civil service</a>. In the western part of Asturias, <a href="/wiki/Eonavian" class="mw-redirect" title="Eonavian">Eonavian</a> is also spoken, and its promotion also falls under the responsibility of Law 1/1998. Whether Eonavian is a <a href="/wiki/Dialect_continuum" title="Dialect continuum">dialect continuum</a> or a variety of <a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">Galician language</a>, however, is a subject of debate, and its use in the Asturian Administration is minor compared to the use of the Asturian language. Within Asturias, there is an ongoing process to establish <a href="/wiki/Place_names" class="mw-redirect" title="Place names">place names</a> in Asturian and Eonavian dialects.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturias&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The organisation and political structure of Asturias is governed by the <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Autonomy_of_the_Principality_of_Asturias" title="Statute of Autonomy of the Principality of Asturias">Statute of Autonomy of the Principality of Asturias</a>, in force since 30 January 1982. According to the Statute, the institutional bodies of the Principality of Asturias are three: the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Government_of_the_Principality_of_Asturias" title="Council of Government of the Principality of Asturias">Council of Government</a>, the <a href="/wiki/General_Junta_of_the_Principality_of_Asturias" title="General Junta of the Principality of Asturias">General Junta</a> and <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Principality_of_Asturias" title="President of the Principality of Asturias">President</a>. The form of government of the Principality is <a href="/wiki/Parliamentarism" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliamentarism">Parliament</a>: The General Junta is the <a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">legislature</a> to choose, on behalf of the Asturian people, the President of the Principality of Asturias. The President is also the one of the Council of Government, the head of <a href="/wiki/Executive_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive power">executive power</a>, and politically answerable to the General Junta.
</p><p>The functions of the General Junta are the approval of budgets, and the direction and control of the action of the Council of Government. It is composed of 45 deputies, elected for four years through theuniversal suffrage within a system proportional representation that the allocation of deputies is based on D'Hondt method.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturias&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Asturian_sheep.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Asturian_sheep.jpg/220px-Asturian_sheep.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Asturian_sheep.jpg/330px-Asturian_sheep.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Asturian_sheep.jpg/440px-Asturian_sheep.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Asturian_sheep.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Asturian sheep on Picos de Europa</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Torre_CCS_Gij%C3%B3n.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Torre_CCS_Gij%C3%B3n.JPG/170px-Torre_CCS_Gij%C3%B3n.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Torre_CCS_Gij%C3%B3n.JPG/255px-Torre_CCS_Gij%C3%B3n.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Torre_CCS_Gij%C3%B3n.JPG/340px-Torre_CCS_Gij%C3%B3n.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1766" data-file-height="2362" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Torre_CCS_Gij%C3%B3n.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>El Musel, the Port of Gijón</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CentroNiemeyer70.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/CentroNiemeyer70.jpg/220px-CentroNiemeyer70.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/CentroNiemeyer70.jpg/330px-CentroNiemeyer70.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/CentroNiemeyer70.jpg/440px-CentroNiemeyer70.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CentroNiemeyer70.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Centro_Niemeyer" class="mw-redirect" title="Centro Niemeyer">Centro Niemeyer</a> designed by <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Niemeyer" title="Oscar Niemeyer">Oscar Niemeyer</a></div></div></div>
<p>For centuries, the backbone of the Asturian economy was <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fishing" title="Fishing">fishing</a>. <a href="/wiki/Milk" title="Milk">Milk</a> production and its derivatives was also traditional, but its big development was a byproduct of the economic expansion of the late 1960s. Nowadays, products from the dairy cooperative Central Lechera Asturiana are being commercialised all over Spain.
</p><p>The main regional industry in modern times, however, was <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">coal</a> mining and <a href="/wiki/Steel" title="Steel">steel</a> production: in the times of Francisco Franco's dictatorship, it was the centre of Spain's steel industry. The then state-owned ENSIDESA steel company is now part of the privatised <a href="/wiki/Aceralia" title="Aceralia">Aceralia</a>, now part of the <a href="/wiki/ArcelorMittal" title="ArcelorMittal">ArcelorMittal</a> Group. The industry created many jobs, which resulted in significant migration from other regions in Spain, mainly <a href="/wiki/Extremadura" title="Extremadura">Extremadura</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">Andalusia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Castile_and_Le%C3%B3n" title="Castile and León">Castile and León</a>.
</p><p>The steel industry is now in decline when measured in terms of number of jobs provided, as is the mining. The reasons for the latter are mainly the high costs of production to extract the coal compared to other regions. Regional economic growth is below the broader Spanish rate, though in recent years growth in service industries has helped reduce Asturias's high rate of unemployment. Large out-of-town retail parks have opened near the region's largest cities (Gijón and Oviedo), whilst the ever-present Spanish construction industry appears to continue to thrive.
</p><p>Asturias has benefited extensively since 1986 from <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> investment in roads and other essential <a href="/wiki/Infrastructure" title="Infrastructure">infrastructure</a>, though there has also been some controversy regarding how these funds are spent, for example, on miners' pensions.
</p><p>As of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Asturias&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the GDP (PPP) per capita of Asturias stood at €22,640, or 90.2% of the European average of €25,100. This makes the region the 12th richest in Spain, a big decrease from the 1970s/1980s - the heyday of the Spanish mining industry, when Asturias was commonly regarded as one of the most prosperous regions in Southern Europe. Asturias has been growing below the Spanish national average since the decline of the mining industry, and grew just 0.82% in 2008, the lowest of all regions in Spain. On the plus side, unemployment in Asturias is below the average of Spain; it stood at 13.7% in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
