<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturias&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:R%C3%A9gional_Embraer_190_F-HBLA_OVD-LEAS.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/R%C3%A9gional_Embraer_190_F-HBLA_OVD-LEAS.jpg/220px-R%C3%A9gional_Embraer_190_F-HBLA_OVD-LEAS.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/R%C3%A9gional_Embraer_190_F-HBLA_OVD-LEAS.jpg/330px-R%C3%A9gional_Embraer_190_F-HBLA_OVD-LEAS.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/R%C3%A9gional_Embraer_190_F-HBLA_OVD-LEAS.jpg/440px-R%C3%A9gional_Embraer_190_F-HBLA_OVD-LEAS.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:R%C3%A9gional_Embraer_190_F-HBLA_OVD-LEAS.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Asturias International Airport</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturias&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Asturias is served by <a href="/wiki/Asturias_Airport" title="Asturias Airport">Asturias International Airport (OVD)</a>, 40 kilometres (25 miles) from Oviedo, near the northwest coast and the industrial town of Avilés.
</p>
<ul><li>International carriers
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Air_France" title="Air France">Air France</a></li>
<li>A British international carrier, <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">EasyJet</a>, began daily flights to Asturias airport in March 2005, it operates to <a href="/wiki/Stansted_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Stansted Airport">Stansted Airport</a>, which the airline uses as a major hub. During the winter period, EasyJet usually reduces flying frequency to four flights per week.</li></ul></li>
<li>Several national carriers also link Asturias to <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seville" title="Seville">Seville</a> and others.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Iberia_Airlines" class="mw-redirect" title="Iberia Airlines">Iberia</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Vueling" title="Vueling">Vueling</a></li></ul></li></ul>
<p>Eastern Asturias is also easily accessible from <a href="/wiki/Santander_Airport" title="Santander Airport">Santander Airport</a>. Recent improvements introduced in the road network permit flying into <a href="/wiki/Santander,_Cantabria" class="mw-redirect" title="Santander, Cantabria">Santander</a> and later driving into Asturias, which can be entered in less than an hour's drive. The Irish airline <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a> operates flights to <a href="/wiki/Santander_Airport" title="Santander Airport">Santander Airport</a> from Frankfurt Hahn, Liverpool, Dublin, Edinburgh, London Stansted and Rome Ciampino.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sea">Sea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturias&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Sea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/El_Musel" title="El Musel">El Musel</a> (the Port of Gijón) is able to receive cruise ships of any size. Companies as P&amp;O, Swan Hellenic or Hapag Lloyd choose the Port of Gijón every year for their calls in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Europe" title="Atlantic Europe">Atlantic European</a> Coast. The following areas are available for cruise vessels:
</p>
<ul><li>Moliner quay: 313 m berthing with 14 m draught.</li>
<li>7ª Alignment: 326 m with 12 m draught.</li>
<li>Espigón II. South alignment. 360 m berth with 9 m draught.</li></ul>
<p>These locations allow a high degree of access control, with security guaranteed for both vessels and passengers alike. The city centre is only 4&#160;km (2.5&#160;mi) away and the Port Authority provides dedicated coach connection allowing passengers to take advantage of the cultural, <a href="/wiki/Gastronomy" title="Gastronomy">gastronomic</a> and commercial opportunities that Gijón has to offer.
</p><p>Since 2010, the city of Gijón is connected by <a href="/wiki/Ferry" title="Ferry">ferry</a> with the French city of <a href="/wiki/Nantes" title="Nantes">Nantes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> This connection is also known as the "sea highway" and it has a frequency of two ferries per day in both directions.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Train">Train</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturias&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Train">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Estacion_Norte_Oviedo_-_Nacho_Gonmi.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Estacion_Norte_Oviedo_-_Nacho_Gonmi.jpg/220px-Estacion_Norte_Oviedo_-_Nacho_Gonmi.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Estacion_Norte_Oviedo_-_Nacho_Gonmi.jpg/330px-Estacion_Norte_Oviedo_-_Nacho_Gonmi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Estacion_Norte_Oviedo_-_Nacho_Gonmi.jpg/440px-Estacion_Norte_Oviedo_-_Nacho_Gonmi.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Estacion_Norte_Oviedo_-_Nacho_Gonmi.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Oviedo Train Station</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Cercan%C3%ADas_Asturias" title="Cercanías Asturias">Cercanías Asturias</a></div>
<p>Spain's national <a href="/wiki/RENFE" class="mw-redirect" title="RENFE">RENFE</a> rail network also serves Asturias well; trains regularly depart to and from the Spanish interior. Major stops are the regional capital, <a href="/wiki/Oviedo" title="Oviedo">Oviedo</a>, and the main coastal city, <a href="/wiki/Gij%C3%B3n" title="Gijón">Gijón</a>. Meanwhile, the <a href="/wiki/FEVE" class="mw-redirect" title="FEVE">FEVE</a> rail company links the centre of the region with Eastern and Western Asturias. Under the <a href="/wiki/Cantabrian_Mountains" title="Cantabrian Mountains">Cantabrian Mountains</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pajares_Base_Tunnel" title="Pajares Base Tunnel">Pajares Base Tunnel</a>, is currently under construction, and will reduce the journey times from Madrid to Asturias from 5 hours to just 3 hours, paving the way for the arrival of <a href="/wiki/AVE" title="AVE">AVE</a> trains in the near future.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bus">Bus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturias&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Bus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There is also a comprehensive bus service run by the <a href="/wiki/ALSA_(bus_company)" title="ALSA (bus company)">ALSA</a> company. It links <a href="/wiki/Avil%C3%A9s" title="Avilés">Avilés</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gij%C3%B3n" title="Gijón">Gijón</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oviedo" title="Oviedo">Oviedo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mieres,_Asturias" class="mw-redirect" title="Mieres, Asturias">Mieres</a> with <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a> and other major towns, several times a day. These include services to <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salamanca" title="Salamanca">Salamanca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Le%C3%B3n_(Spain)" class="mw-redirect" title="León (Spain)">León</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valladolid" title="Valladolid">Valladolid</a>, <a href="/wiki/A_Coru%C3%B1a" title="A Coruña">A Coruña</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bilbao" title="Bilbao">Bilbao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seville" title="Seville">Seville</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Sebasti%C3%A1n" title="San Sebastián">San Sebastián</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nice" title="Nice">Nice</a>, to name just a few.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Main_sights">Main sights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturias&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Main sights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Oviedo-Catedral.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Oviedo-Catedral.JPG/170px-Oviedo-Catedral.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Oviedo-Catedral.JPG/255px-Oviedo-Catedral.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Oviedo-Catedral.JPG/340px-Oviedo-Catedral.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1704" data-file-height="2272" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Oviedo-Catedral.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_San_Salvador,_Oviedo" class="mw-redirect" title="Cathedral of San Salvador, Oviedo">The Oviedo Cathedral</a>. Built from 781 to 16th century.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:La_santa_cueva.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/La_santa_cueva.jpg/220px-La_santa_cueva.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/La_santa_cueva.jpg/330px-La_santa_cueva.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/La_santa_cueva.jpg/440px-La_santa_cueva.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1365" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:La_santa_cueva.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Holy_Cave_of_Covadonga" class="mw-redirect" title="Holy Cave of Covadonga">Holy Cave of Covadonga</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cudillero_Asturias.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Cudillero_Asturias.jpg/220px-Cudillero_Asturias.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Cudillero_Asturias.jpg/330px-Cudillero_Asturias.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Cudillero_Asturias.jpg/440px-Cudillero_Asturias.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cudillero_Asturias.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The village of <a href="/wiki/Cudillero" title="Cudillero">Cudillero</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2482-Puente_romano_en_Cangas_de_Onis_(Asturias).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/2482-Puente_romano_en_Cangas_de_Onis_%28Asturias%29.jpg/220px-2482-Puente_romano_en_Cangas_de_Onis_%28Asturias%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/2482-Puente_romano_en_Cangas_de_Onis_%28Asturias%29.jpg/330px-2482-Puente_romano_en_Cangas_de_Onis_%28Asturias%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/2482-Puente_romano_en_Cangas_de_Onis_%28Asturias%29.jpg/440px-2482-Puente_romano_en_Cangas_de_Onis_%28Asturias%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2956" data-file-height="2244" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2482-Puente_romano_en_Cangas_de_Onis_(Asturias).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Roman Bridge of Cangas de Onís</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Key_attractions">Key attractions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturias&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Key attractions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Oviedo" title="Oviedo">Oviedo</a> is the capital city of Asturias and contains <a href="/wiki/Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_del_Naranco" title="Santa María del Naranco">Santa María del Naranco</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Miguel_de_Lillo" title="San Miguel de Lillo">San Miguel de Lillo</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Pre-Romanesque" class="mw-redirect" title="Pre-Romanesque">pre-Romanesque</a> church and a palace respectively, which were built by the first Asturian kings on Mount Naranco, to the north of the city (<a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>). In modern architecture, the <i>Palacio de Congresos de Oviedo</i> (or <i>Modoo</i>) was designed by <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Calatrava" title="Santiago Calatrava">Santiago Calatrava</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Gijon" class="mw-redirect" title="Gijon">Gijon</a>, the biggest city of Asturias, is a coastal city known for cultural and sports events,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and a beach tourism centre in northern Spain. It also is known for the traditional Asturian gastronomy and for being an Asturian cider production spot.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Museums in the city include the <b><a href="/wiki/Universidad_Laboral_de_Gij%C3%B3n" title="Universidad Laboral de Gijón">Universidad Laboral de Gijón</a></b>, including a modern art museum and theatre.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Avil%C3%A9s" title="Avilés">Avilés</a> is the third largest city in Asturias, where "La villa del adelantado" (as locals call it, in reference of <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Men%C3%A9ndez_de_Avil%C3%A9s" title="Pedro Menéndez de Avilés">Pedro Menéndez de Avilés</a>) is a meeting point. "Saint Nicholas of Bari" or "Capilla de los Alas" in Romanesque and Romanesque-Gothic style, respectively; Palacio de Balsera, in Modernist style or St. Thomas of Canterbury church (dating from the 13th century) are examples which show the historical patrimony to be found in the city.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Niemeyer_International_Cultural_Centre" title="Oscar Niemeyer International Cultural Centre">Centro Niemeyer</a>, designed by the Brazilian architect <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Niemeyer" title="Oscar Niemeyer">Oscar Niemeyer</a>, is an example of contemporary architecture in Asturias.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Picos_de_Europa" title="Picos de Europa">Picos de Europa</a> National Park, and other parts of the Asturian mountain range: The Picu Urriellu mountain (2519 m or 8262&#160;ft), also known as <i>El Naranjo de Bulnes</i>, is a molar-shaped peak which, reputedly, glows orange in the evening sun, hence its name. Weather permitting, it can be viewed from Camarmeña village, near Poncebos, south of Arenas de Cabrales.
</p><p>The shrine to the Virgin of <a href="/wiki/Covadonga" title="Covadonga">Covadonga</a> and the mountain lakes (<i><a href="/wiki/Lakes_of_Covadonga" title="Lakes of Covadonga">Los Lagos</a></i>), near <a href="/wiki/Cangas_de_On%C3%ADs" title="Cangas de Onís">Cangas de Onís</a>: Legend has it that in the 8th century, the <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Covadonga" title="Our Lady of Covadonga">Virgin</a> blessed Asturian Christian forces with a well-timed signal to attack Spain's Moorish conquerors, thereby taking the invaders by surprise in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Covadonga" title="Battle of Covadonga">Battle of Covadonga</a>. The <i><a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">Reconquista</a></i> and eventual unification of all Spain is therefore said to have started in this very location.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The paleolithic art in the caves of Asturias is declared <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Cave_of_Altamira_and_Paleolithic_Cave_Art_of_Northern_Spain" title="Cave of Altamira and Paleolithic Cave Art of Northern Spain">Paleolithic Art of Northern Spain</a>.
</p><p>Asturias also has examples of <a href="/wiki/Industrial_archaeology" title="Industrial archaeology">industrial heritage</a> as a consequence of its industrial activities in the 19th and 20th centuries. It had metallurgical and chemical factories, mines, bridges and railways, including in the towns of <a href="/wiki/Langreo" title="Langreo">Langreo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mieres" title="Mieres">Mieres</a> and <a href="/wiki/Avil%C3%A9s" title="Avilés">Avilés</a>.
</p><p>The Asturian coast: especially the beaches in and around the summer resort of <a href="/wiki/Llanes" title="Llanes">Llanes</a>, the Playa del Silencio near <a href="/wiki/Cudillero" title="Cudillero">Cudillero</a> fishing village, or the "white" village of <a href="/wiki/Luarca" title="Luarca">Luarca</a> (<a href="/wiki/Severo_Ochoa" title="Severo Ochoa">Severo Ochoa</a> hometown).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_places_of_interest">Other places of interest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturias&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Other places of interest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Somiedo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Somiedo.jpg/220px-Somiedo.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Somiedo.jpg/330px-Somiedo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Somiedo.jpg/440px-Somiedo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Somiedo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Somiedo Lake</div></div></div>
<ul><li>Ceceda village: east of <a href="/wiki/Oviedo" title="Oviedo">Oviedo</a> along the N634 road. Of particular interest in this exemplary settlement are the traditional <i><a href="/wiki/H%C3%B3rreo" title="Hórreo">horreos</a></i> (grain silos), raised on stilts so as to keep field mice from getting at the grain.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Dobra_(Sella)" title="Dobra (Sella)">Dobra River</a>: south of <a href="/wiki/Cangas_de_On%C3%ADs" title="Cangas de Onís">Cangas de Onís</a>, known for its unusual colour.</li>
<li>The <i>senda costera</i> (coastal way) between Pendueles and <a href="/wiki/Llanes" title="Llanes">Llanes</a>: This partly paved nature route takes in some of Asturias' most spectacular coastal scenery, such as the noisy <i>bufones</i> (<a href="/wiki/Blowhole_(geology)" title="Blowhole (geology)">blowholes</a>) and the Playa de <a href="/wiki/Ballota_(Cudillero)" title="Ballota (Cudillero)">Ballota</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Caldoveiro_Peak" title="Caldoveiro Peak">Caldoveiro Peak</a>, a scenic mountain hiking area</li>
<li>The unusual rock formation on the beach at Buelna village: east of <a href="/wiki/Llanes" title="Llanes">Llanes</a>. Best viewed at low tide.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturias&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturias&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Asturias&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">June 2015</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Asturias has a rich artistic legacy that emphasizes <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_art" title="Romanesque art">Romanesque</a> (<i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturias_Arts&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Asturias Arts (page does not exist)">Asturias Arts</a></i>) indigenous architecture with monuments like <a href="/wiki/Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_del_Naranco" title="Santa María del Naranco">Santa María del Naranco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cristina_de_Lena" title="Santa Cristina de Lena">Santa Cristina de Lena</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Miguel_de_Lillo" title="San Miguel de Lillo">San Miguel de Lillo</a>. These monuments have a Ramirense Romanesque style (due to <a href="/wiki/Ramiro_I_of_Asturias" title="Ramiro I of Asturias">Ramiro I</a>) or <a href="/wiki/San_Juli%C3%A1n_de_los_Prados" title="San Julián de los Prados">San Julián de los Prados</a>, known as Santullano (<a href="/wiki/Oviedo" title="Oviedo">Oviedo</a>) of the Alfonsino pre-Romanesque style (due to <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_II_of_Asturias" title="Alfonso II of Asturias">Alfonso II</a>), which are all in Oviedo. Other examples of architecture are Villaviciosa's church, <a href="/wiki/San_Salvador_de_Valdedi%C3%B3s" class="mw-redirect" title="San Salvador de Valdediós">San Salvador de Valdediós</a> (commonly known by the Asturians as "Conventín"), and the church of San Salvador de Priesca. Another example is <a href="/wiki/Cabranes" title="Cabranes">Cabranes'</a> <a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Julian_de_Vi%C3%B1%C3%B3n&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="San Julian de Viñón (page does not exist)">San Julian de Viñón</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_architecture" title="Romanesque architecture">Romanesque</a> style is very present, since all Asturias is crossed by one of the <a href="/wiki/Camino_de_Santiago" title="Camino de Santiago">Camino de Santiago</a> routes, which highlights the <a href="/wiki/Monastery_of_San_Pedro_de_Villanueva" title="Monastery of San Pedro de Villanueva">Monastery of San Pedro de Villanueva</a> (near <a href="/wiki/Cangas_de_Onis" class="mw-redirect" title="Cangas de Onis">Cangas de Onis</a>), the churches of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Church_of_San_Esteban_(Aramil)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Church of San Esteban (Aramil) (page does not exist)">San Esteban de Aramil</a> (<a href="/wiki/Siero" title="Siero">Siero</a>), <a href="/w/index.php?title=Church_of_San_Juan_(Amandi)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Church of San Juan (Amandi) (page does not exist)">San Juan de Amandi</a> (<a href="/wiki/Villaviciosa,_Asturias" title="Villaviciosa, Asturias">Villaviciosa</a>) and Santa María de Junco (<a href="/wiki/Ribadesella" title="Ribadesella">Ribadesella</a>).
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">Gothic</a> style is not as abundant, but there are good examples of this style, such as the <a href="/wiki/Oviedo_Cathedral" title="Oviedo Cathedral">Cathedral of San Salvador</a> in Oviedo.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Baroque_architecture" title="Baroque architecture">Baroque</a> style is more present by means of palace architecture, with such notable examples as the Palace of Camposagrado and Velarde - the latter seat of <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Fine_Arts_of_Asturias" title="Museum of Fine Arts of Asturias">Museum of Fine Arts of Asturias</a>. The Baroque style stands out in public civil engineering and bridge tolls (<a href="/wiki/Olloniego" title="Olloniego">Olloniego</a>); the milestones, the chairs or seats present along the road to Madrid and the resort of Caldas de Priorio (Oviedo) building.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CentroNiemeyer92.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/CentroNiemeyer92.jpg/220px-CentroNiemeyer92.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/CentroNiemeyer92.jpg/330px-CentroNiemeyer92.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/CentroNiemeyer92.jpg/440px-CentroNiemeyer92.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CentroNiemeyer92.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Oscar_Niemeyer_International_Cultural_Centre" title="Oscar Niemeyer International Cultural Centre">Oscar Niemeyer International Cultural Centre</a></div></div></div>
<p>In 1985, the <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> declared the pre-Romanesque monuments and the <a href="/wiki/Oviedo_Cathedral" title="Oviedo Cathedral">Cathedral of Oviedo</a> as <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Sites</a>.
</p><p>In popular architecture, the traditional granaries in Asturias, called <i><a href="/wiki/H%C3%B3rreo" title="Hórreo">hórreos</a></i>, are known for their demographic extension and their functional evolution, its basic characteristic being its mobility: it can be easily dismounted and transported to another location. The <a href="/wiki/Panera" class="mw-redirect" title="Panera">Panera</a> is the evolution of the hórreo, with examples exceeding 100 square metres (1,076 square feet) of area covered. The purpose of the horreo is to store objects and crops. With the arrival of maize and the beans, they were endowed with exterior corridors and railings for drying the harvests.
</p><p>Asturias is home to the only architectural work in Spain (as well as the largest in Europe) of the Brazilian architect and disciple of <a href="/wiki/Le_Corbusier" title="Le Corbusier">Le Corbusier</a>; <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Niemeyer" title="Oscar Niemeyer">Oscar Niemeyer</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Niemeyer_International_Cultural_Centre" title="Oscar Niemeyer International Cultural Centre">Oscar Niemeyer International Cultural Centre</a>. The architectural project was donated to the Principality by the architect, who was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Asturias_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Prince of Asturias Award">Prince of Asturias Award for the Arts</a>, in the XXV edition of these awards. Niemeyer's project combined several different elements, and projected an open space, a place for education, culture and peace.
</p><p>In the capital of the Principality stands one of the most representative buildings of modern architecture, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Palace_of_Congresses_of_Oviedo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Palace of Congresses of Oviedo (page does not exist)">Palace of Congresses of Oviedo</a>, by the Spanish architect <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Calatrava" title="Santiago Calatrava">Santiago Calatrava</a>, who also awarded the Prince of Asturias of Award for the Arts in 1999.
</p><p>Special importance has been placed in recent years on the recovery of <a href="/wiki/Industrial_heritage" title="Industrial heritage">industrial heritage</a> through various routes and industrial museums, especially in the central area of the region.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Festivals_and_holidays">Festivals and holidays</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturias&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Festivals and holidays">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Some of the most famous festivals in Asturias are from the small town of <a href="/wiki/Llanes" title="Llanes">Llanes</a>. These festivals celebrate the important saints and the Virgin Mary adored by the town. The associations that prepare the festivals have a rivalry between them and each year they try to outdo each other with more impressive shows. The three most important are the festival of San Roque (St. Roque) held on the 16th of August, the festival of Nuestra Señora Virgen de La Guia (Our Lady, Virgin Mary, the Guide) held on the 8th of September, and the festival of Santa Maria Magdalena (St. Mary Magdalene) held on the 22nd of July. The Magdalena is well known for its impressive march of logs where boys as young as 3 and men carry logs through the town until they reach the end point and start a large bonfire.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Traditional_Asturian_Dress.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Traditional_Asturian_Dress.jpg/170px-Traditional_Asturian_Dress.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="247" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Traditional_Asturian_Dress.jpg/255px-Traditional_Asturian_Dress.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Traditional_Asturian_Dress.jpg/340px-Traditional_Asturian_Dress.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1077" data-file-height="1563" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Traditional_Asturian_Dress.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Traditional Asturian dress being worn during a major festival in <a href="/wiki/Llanes" title="Llanes">Llanes</a></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food_and_drink">Food and drink</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturias&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Food and drink">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Asturian_cuisine" title="Asturian cuisine">Asturian cuisine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fabada_y_sidra.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Fabada_y_sidra.jpg/220px-Fabada_y_sidra.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Fabada_y_sidra.jpg/330px-Fabada_y_sidra.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Fabada_y_sidra.jpg/440px-Fabada_y_sidra.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1632" data-file-height="1224" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fabada_y_sidra.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Fabada asturiana</i> and sidra (cider), a typical dish of Asturias</div></div></div>
<p>While Asturias is especially known for its <a href="/wiki/Seafood" title="Seafood">seafood</a>, the most famous regional dish is <i><a href="/wiki/Fabada_Asturiana" class="mw-redirect" title="Fabada Asturiana">fabada asturiana</a></i>, a rich stew typically made with large white <a href="/wiki/Broad_bean" class="mw-redirect" title="Broad bean">beans</a> (<i>fabes</i>), shoulder of <a href="/wiki/Pork" title="Pork">pork</a> (<i>lacón</i>), black pudding (<i><a href="/wiki/Morcilla" class="mw-redirect" title="Morcilla">morcilla</a></i>), and spicy <a href="/wiki/Sausage" title="Sausage">sausage</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Chorizo" title="Chorizo">chorizo</a></i>).
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Apple" title="Apple">Apple</a> groves foster the production of the region's traditional alcoholic drink, a natural <a href="/wiki/Cider" title="Cider">cider</a> (<i>sidra</i>). Since it is natural and bottled without gas, it produces a weak carbonation, and when Asturian cider is served, it is poured in a particular way, <i>el escanciado</i>: the bottle is held above the head allowing for a long vertical pour, causing the cider to be aerated as it splashes into the glass below. After drinking most of the content, it is customary to splash a little out onto the ground, as a way to clean the glass of any <a href="/wiki/Lees_(fermentation)" title="Lees (fermentation)">lees</a> for the next serving. Traditionally, the same glass is refilled and passed around, with everyone drinking from it in turn.
</p><p>Asturian <a href="/wiki/Cheese" title="Cheese">cheeses</a>, especially <a href="/wiki/Cabrales_cheese" title="Cabrales cheese">Cabrales</a>, are also eaten throughout Spain and beyond; Asturias is often called "the land of cheeses" (<i>el país de los quesos</i>).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturias&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Asturias" title="Sport in Asturias">Sport in Asturias</a></div>
<p>Asturias has two main football teams: <a href="/wiki/Real_Sporting_de_Gij%C3%B3n" class="mw-redirect" title="Real Sporting de Gijón">Sporting de Gijón</a> and <a href="/wiki/Real_Oviedo" title="Real Oviedo">Real Oviedo</a>, which have played over 35 seasons in <a href="/wiki/La_Liga" title="La Liga">La Liga</a>. Other current notable sports teams are <a href="/wiki/Oviedo_CB" title="Oviedo CB">Oviedo CB</a> (basketball) and <a href="/wiki/AB_Gij%C3%B3n_Jovellanos" title="AB Gijón Jovellanos">AB Gijón Jovellanos</a> (handball).
</p><p>Racecar driver <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Alonso" title="Fernando Alonso">Fernando Alonso</a> is a two-time <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a> world champion, and races with Asturias' flag colours on his helmet. Also, cyclist <a href="/wiki/Samuel_S%C3%A1nchez" title="Samuel Sánchez">Samuel Sánchez</a> won a gold at the Olympic games. Football players from Asturias include World Cup winner <a href="/wiki/David_Villa" title="David Villa">David Villa</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Quini" title="Quini">Quini</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luis_Enrique_(footballer)" title="Luis Enrique (footballer)">Luis Enrique</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juan_Manuel_Mata" class="mw-redirect" title="Juan Manuel Mata">Juan Manuel Mata</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Cazorla" class="mw-redirect" title="Santiago Cazorla">Santiago Cazorla</a>, among others.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturias&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturias&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Al_son_de_la_gaita.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Al_son_de_la_gaita.jpg/170px-Al_son_de_la_gaita.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Al_son_de_la_gaita.jpg/255px-Al_son_de_la_gaita.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Al_son_de_la_gaita.jpg/340px-Al_son_de_la_gaita.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1704" data-file-height="2272" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Al_son_de_la_gaita.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Gaita_asturiana" title="Gaita asturiana">Gaita asturiana</a></i>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Estaci%C3%B3n_de_Valgrande-Pajares.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Estaci%C3%B3n_de_Valgrande-Pajares.JPG/170px-Estaci%C3%B3n_de_Valgrande-Pajares.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Estaci%C3%B3n_de_Valgrande-Pajares.JPG/255px-Estaci%C3%B3n_de_Valgrande-Pajares.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Estaci%C3%B3n_de_Valgrande-Pajares.JPG/340px-Estaci%C3%B3n_de_Valgrande-Pajares.JPG 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Estaci%C3%B3n_de_Valgrande-Pajares.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Valgrande-Pajares ski resort</div></div></div>
<p>The music of Asturias is varied. The most characteristic instrument in traditional music is the <a href="/wiki/Gaita_asturiana" title="Gaita asturiana">Asturian bagpipe</a>, or <i>Gaita asturiana</i>, which has a single drone, in common with the traditional bagpipes of other Celtic nations such as Wales and Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> The bagpipe is often accompanied by the hand drum, whistles and accordion.
</p><p>In recent years, there has been a resurgence of interest in traditional folk music, and several music ensembles have gained regional and international recognition for their ethnomusicological study and presentation of indigenous Asturian music.  Notable examples include traditional pipers such as Xuacu Amieva and Tejedor and fusionist José Ángel <a href="/wiki/Hevia" title="Hevia">Hevia</a> (whose music video<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> provides views of both the gaita and the Asturian landscape), and the groups <a href="/wiki/Llan_de_Cubel" title="Llan de Cubel">Llan de Cubel</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Xera_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Xera (band) (page does not exist)">Xera</a>, Nuberu and Felpeyu.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Additionally, numerous rock, ska and heavy metal groups have also found relative success within Asturias, many of which incorporate elements of traditional Asturian music into their sound.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Anthem">Anthem</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturias&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Anthem">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Asturian anthem <a href="/wiki/Asturias,_patria_querida" title="Asturias, patria querida">Asturias, patria querida</a> (Asturias, beloved fatherland), which was a popular song adopted as the region's anthem and formalised by <i>Ley 1/1984, de 27 de Abríl</i>.
</p>
<h3><span id="Orquesta_Sinf.C3.B3nica_del_Principado_de_Asturias"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Orquesta_Sinfónica_del_Principado_de_Asturias">Orquesta Sinfónica del Principado de Asturias</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturias&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Orquesta Sinfónica del Principado de Asturias">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Orquesta_Sinfonica_del_Principado_de_Asturias&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Orquesta Sinfonica del Principado de Asturias (page does not exist)">Orquesta Sinfónica del Principado de Asturias</a> is the premier orchestra in the Principality of Asturias.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> It is based in the Auditorio Príncipe Felipe in Oviedo, but also performs in the main concert venues in Gijón and Avilés. <a href="/wiki/Rossen_Milanov" title="Rossen Milanov">Rossen Milanov</a> is the Music Director.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other">Other</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturias&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Other">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Leyenda" class="mw-redirect" title="Leyenda">Asturias</a></i> is also the name of the fifth movement of the <i>Suite Española, Op. 47</i> by Spanish composer <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Alb%C3%A9niz" title="Isaac Albéniz">Isaac Albéniz</a>. Nevertheless, the music has little in common with the region's own folklore. More authentic is Rimsky Korsakov's <i>Spanish Capriccio</i>, which quotes liberally from Asturian musical heritage.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturias&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Asturians" title="Asturians">Asturians</a></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Luis_Enrique_Mart%C3%ADnez_Garc%C3%ADa" class="mw-redirect" title="Luis Enrique Martínez García">Luis Enrique Martínez García</a>, former <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">FC Barcelona</a> captain and manager. he has also been the manager of <a href="/wiki/Spain_national_football_team" title="Spain national football team">Spain national football team</a> since July 9, 2018.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Juan_Carre%C3%B1o_de_Miranda" title="Juan Carreño de Miranda">Juan Carreño de Miranda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Court_painter" title="Court painter">court painter</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fernando_Alonso" title="Fernando Alonso">Fernando Alonso</a>, <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a> racing driver, 2005 and 2006 world champion</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Leopoldo_Alas" title="Leopoldo Alas">Leopoldo Alas</a> "Clarín", 19th-century author of <i>La Regenta</i>, a seminal work in the Spanish literary canon</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Armando_Palacio_Vald%C3%A9s" title="Armando Palacio Valdés">Armando Palacio Valdés</a>, 19th and 20th-century novelist and critic</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Francisco_%C3%81lvarez_Cascos" class="mw-redirect" title="Francisco Álvarez Cascos">Francisco Álvarez Cascos</a>, minister in Spain's government 1996–2000 and 2000–2004</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Santi_Cazorla" title="Santi Cazorla">Santi Cazorla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C" class="mw-redirect" title="Arsenal F.C">Arsenal</a> and Spain international football player, European Champion 2008 and 2012</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Torcuato_Fern%C3%A1ndez-Miranda" title="Torcuato Fernández-Miranda">Torcuato Fernández-Miranda</a>, key lawmaker during the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_transition_to_democracy" title="Spanish transition to democracy">Spanish transition to democracy</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/%C3%81ngel_Gonz%C3%A1lez_Mu%C3%B1iz" title="Ángel González Muñiz">Ángel González</a>, major Spanish poet of the 20th century.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gaspar_Melchor_de_Jovellanos" title="Gaspar Melchor de Jovellanos">Gaspar Melchor de Jovellanos</a>, philosopher, politician, <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Enlightenment" title="Age of Enlightenment">Enlightenment</a> thinker</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pedro_Men%C3%A9ndez_de_Avil%C3%A9s" title="Pedro Menéndez de Avilés">Pedro Menéndez de Avilés</a> Spanish explorer and founder of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Augustine,_Florida" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Augustine, Florida">Saint Augustine, Florida</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Queen_Letizia_of_Spain" title="Queen Letizia of Spain">Queen Letizia of Spain</a>, a native of <a href="/wiki/Oviedo" title="Oviedo">Oviedo</a> and wife of <a href="/wiki/Felipe_VI_of_Spain" title="Felipe VI of Spain">Felipe VI, King of Spain</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Severo_Ochoa" title="Severo Ochoa">Severo Ochoa</a>, 1959 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a> winner for physiology or medicine</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Carmen_Polo" class="mw-redirect" title="Carmen Polo">Carmen Polo</a>, wife of Spanish dictator Francisco Franco</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chechu_Rubiera" class="mw-redirect" title="Chechu Rubiera">Chechu Rubiera</a>, cyclist</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Andr%C3%A9s" title="José Andrés">José Andrés</a>, chef</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Amalia_Ulman" title="Amalia Ulman">Amalia Ulman</a>, artist</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/David_Villa" title="David Villa">David Villa</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_FC" title="New York City FC">New York City FC</a> and Spain international football star, European Champion 2008, World Champion 2010</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Juan_Manuel_Mata" class="mw-redirect" title="Juan Manuel Mata">Juan Manuel Mata</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United F.C.</a> player, Spain international football star, World Champion 2010 and European Champion 2012</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Michu" title="Michu">Michu</a>, former <a href="/wiki/Swansea_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Swansea City">Swansea City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rayo_Vallecano" title="Rayo Vallecano">Rayo Vallecano</a> player</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Xaviel_Vilareyo" title="Xaviel Vilareyo">Xaviel Vilareyo</a>, national poet, writer and musician</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Samuel_S%C3%A1nchez" title="Samuel Sánchez">Samuel Sánchez</a>, cyclist, Olympic gold medalist</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Melendi" title="Melendi">Melendi</a>, is a Spanish pop singer-songwriter</li></ul>
